  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d07599cb-8da0-4a4f-b18b-07ab6df07a21'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText12279743732214066546" style="display:none">Georgie McCool knows her marriage is in trouble; it has been in trouble for a long time. She still loves her husband, Neal, and Neal still loves her, deeply — but that almost seems beside the point now.<br /><br />Maybe that was always beside the point.<br /><br />Two days before they’re supposed to visit Neal’s family in Omaha for Christmas, Georgie tells Neal that she can’t go. She’s a TV writer, and something’s come up on her show; she has to stay in Los Angeles. She knows that Neal will be upset with her — Neal is always a little upset with Georgie — but she doesn't expect him to pack up the kids and go home without her.<br /><br />When her husband and the kids leave for the airport, Georgie wonders if she’s finally done it. If she’s ruined everything.<br /><br />That night, Georgie discovers a way to communicate with Neal in the past. It’s not time travel, not exactly, but she feels like she’s been given an opportunity to fix her marriage before it starts...<br /><br />Is that what she’s supposed to do?<br /><br />Or would Georgie and Neal be better off if their marriage never happened?</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Absolutely not! This is in no way a good book to try and get back into the romance genre. This is in no way a good book to try and get back into the romance genre. The writing is juvenile, all the characters are unlikeable, and ultimately the whole story unbelievable. I'm just annoyed at myself for having wasted time reading the whole thing. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/924501414?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikki Plummer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikki Plummer" href="/user/show/7844176-nikki-plummer">Nikki Plummer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer924501414" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16080177202153389407">I've loved all Rainbow Rowell's other books, but this one just didn't do it for me. The premise was ridiculous and I hated pretty much every character except Heather. Especially Neal, GOD I hated Neal, what an awful, miserable person. I'm really confused as to how he's supposed to be an appealing character since he's not even described with any redeeming qualities really - an unattractive guy who never laughs, smiles or expresses his feelings in any way, apart from just silently projecting miser</span>
  <span id="freeText16080177202153389407" style="display:none">I've loved all Rainbow Rowell's other books, but this one just didn't do it for me. The premise was ridiculous and I hated pretty much every character except Heather. Especially Neal, GOD I hated Neal, what an awful, miserable person. I'm really confused as to how he's supposed to be an appealing character since he's not even described with any redeeming qualities really - an unattractive guy who never laughs, smiles or expresses his feelings in any way, apart from just silently projecting misery and resentment at his wife without ever actually bringing up the fact that anything is wrong. Every woman's dream! I couldn't understand why Georgie would have even wanted to marry him in the first place, let alone save their marriage which sounds horrible and depressing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16080177202153389407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_644808148" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/644808148" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/644808148?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=addictive">addictive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=christmas">christmas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=romantical">romantical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=books-about-writers">books-about-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=wibbly-wobbly-timey-wimey">wibbly-wobbly-timey-wimey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=speculative">speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close">not-quite-five-stars-but-sooo-close</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644808148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer836409955969509744"><b>Re-Read Review March 16, 2019</b>: Still good, but not my fave of hers. Like, 4.5 stars. If I had to rate all her books, this one would be nearer to the bottom, just above <i>Eleanor & Park</i>, and that's purely personal preference speaking. All of the Rowells are Quality. (I have no idea what to expect for the forthcoming <i>Pumpkinheads</i>, but I am nevertheless excited in my ignorance.)<br/><br/>This is definitely the most adult of her books, not a true romance, but a story of marriage and the hard work and heartbreak</span>
  <span id="freeText836409955969509744" style="display:none"><b>Re-Read Review March 16, 2019</b>: Still good, but not my fave of hers. Like, 4.5 stars. If I had to rate all her books, this one would be nearer to the bottom, just above <i>Eleanor &amp; Park</i>, and that's purely personal preference speaking. All of the Rowells are Quality. (I have no idea what to expect for the forthcoming <i>Pumpkinheads</i>, but I am nevertheless excited in my ignorance.)<br /><br />This is definitely the most adult of her books, not a true romance, but a story of marriage and the hard work and heartbreak that goes into it. Not being married, I can't relate specifically, but this book feels personal in that "I opened up a vein to write this" sort of way, and that gets to you as a reader.<br /><br />Georgie and Neil are both Pieces of Work (in different ways), and I'm not sure I really *like* them, but I do feel for them and I want them to be happy. I still love the main conceit of this book, that inexplicable magical telephone that's never explained, but just descends into Georgie's life like judgment from on high: Talk to your husband. They stopped really talking to each long before we enter their lives, and it seems very fitting and circular (story-wise) that the main thrust of this book is Georgie talking herself back into her relationship by talking to Neil from the past, simultaneously convincing him in the past to do something she never knew she'd convinced him to do in the first place. TIME TRAVEL!<br /><br />Seth is gross and I don't like him.<br /><br />The little romance subplot in this (f/f) is one of my favorite things Rainbow has ever written, and how they finally get together is the most adorable and sort of gross (puppies!). I know she can write m/m romance and m/f, so I would like her please to maybe try to write a full novel of f/f. I bet she would be great at it.<br /><br />This concludes my review that I should have written a month and a half ago.<br /><br />[4.5 stars]</span>
  <a data-text-id="836409955969509744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791887767?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=2014-publication">2014-publication</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=skimmed-or-unfinished">skimmed-or-unfinished</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791887767" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1654206942994043768"><b>DNF</b> about halfway through. As always, I like the author's narrative voice, but as a character sketch of a marriage, this wasn't quite sharp enough or funny enough or emotional enough for my taste. I also find Georgie's profession rather jarring, in that it was rather unrealistically portrayed in both the details and in Georgie's character. Had I never read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty' title='Liane Moriarty' rel='nofollow noopener'>Liane Moriarty</a>, who writes excellent books that humorously dissect marriages and relationships, and had I never worked in entertainment, I mi</span>
  <span id="freeText1654206942994043768" style="display:none"><b>DNF</b> about halfway through. As always, I like the author's narrative voice, but as a character sketch of a marriage, this wasn't quite sharp enough or funny enough or emotional enough for my taste. I also find Georgie's profession rather jarring, in that it was rather unrealistically portrayed in both the details and in Georgie's character. Had I never read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/322069.Liane_Moriarty" title="Liane Moriarty" rel="nofollow noopener">Liane Moriarty</a>, who writes excellent books that humorously dissect marriages and relationships, and had I never worked in entertainment, I might've liked this one better.<br /><br />Oh! And the only thing more tedious than being forced into phone conversations with young kids you don't have a relationship with is having to read about them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1654206942994043768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_761133480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761133480" />
    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530557165p2/6536286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761133480?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781409154914" href="/book/show/21869936-landline">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761133480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12503458913311186732">Since this book hasn't been released yet (MWAHAHA I READ IT BEFORE EVERYONE!) I'm not going to say too much here, but I will be mentioning it on my channel closer to the release date. For now, here is a little blurb of my thoughts:<br/><br/>This was a really different read, and I realized when finishing it that a big part of that is because it is NOT Young Adult. The cover looks it, Rainbow Rowell writes young adult, but this is adult and it shows. It's darker, it's more realistic, and it's less idealisti</span>
  <span id="freeText12503458913311186732" style="display:none">Since this book hasn't been released yet (MWAHAHA I READ IT BEFORE EVERYONE!) I'm not going to say too much here, but I will be mentioning it on my channel closer to the release date. For now, here is a little blurb of my thoughts:<br /><br />This was a really different read, and I realized when finishing it that a big part of that is because it is NOT Young Adult. The cover looks it, Rainbow Rowell writes young adult, but this is adult and it shows. It's darker, it's more realistic, and it's less idealistic. And that's not bad at all, but it's sadder. The book started off harsher and the pay off wasn't as extravagant. All of that in mind, this book was wonderful. The characters were complex and unique and real, and their relationships where layered and difficult and full of history. The magical element in this book was a mixture of stressful and crazy exciting. And the main characters struggle was beautiful.<br /><br />I'm glad I read this, and I'm especially (MWAHAHAHA) glad I read it early, and I definitely recommend it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12503458913311186732" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1452539567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1452539567" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1452539567?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1452539567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14482493519141927074"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You don't know when you're twenty-three.<br/><br/>You don't know what it really means to crawl into someone else's life and stay there. You can't see all the ways you're going to get tangled, how you're going to bond skin to skin. How the idea of separating will feel in five years, in ten -- in fifteen...<br/><br/>She didn't know it at twenty-three."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>This book guys. <b>THIS BOOK.</b> I finished this book in a handful amount of hours in <b>
  <u>one sitting.</u>
</b> Now I know why everybody seems to praise Rainbow Rowell so</span>
  <span id="freeText14482493519141927074" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"You don't know when you're twenty-three.<br /><br />You don't know what it really means to crawl into someone else's life and stay there. You can't see all the ways you're going to get tangled, how you're going to bond skin to skin. How the idea of separating will feel in five years, in ten -- in fifteen...<br /><br />She didn't know it at twenty-three."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />This book guys. <b>THIS BOOK.</b> I finished this book in a handful amount of hours in <b>
  <u>one sitting.</u>
</b> Now I know why everybody seems to praise Rainbow Rowell so much. She's absolutely <b>
  <i>amazing.</i>
</b> Her writing is just so simple and easy to read. The story was fast-paced, cute, and bittersweet. I loved everything about it. I was already hooked after the first page. I honestly wonder how in the world the ratings for Landline aren't much higher!<br /><br />I always wondered what I would do when put in a similar situation as Georgie where I had to choose between my <i>career or my family.</i> Each time my answer is always the same: <b>
  <i>Why can't I have both?</i>
</b> Every book, every movie, or every show that models the same predicament debating which is of more importance (career or family), always seems to propose an either-or solution. <b>
  <i>Where's the compromise?</i>
</b> There has to be a solution in which both sides can win. But then again, if Georgie and Neal thought of a compromising solution at that time, this book wouldn't have came into existence so I won't complain much further. :D<br /><br />This book made me cry. YES. <b>
  <u>CRY.</u>
</b> It was just so darn cute and adorable and sad and just ugh. I was crying because I seriously couldn't handle all the <b>
  <i>feels</i>
</b> that Landline gave me. How in the world does that even happen? Guys, seriously though. I was <b>bawling.</b> And depressed. Because it was so <i>bittersweet and cute.</i><br /><br />I didn't even expect this to be a <b>
  <i>Christmas-y</i>
</b> type of story but I'm so glad I just spontaneously decided to read it because it brought so much holiday cheer and tears to my heart.<br /><br />Landline is the cutest thing I've ever read and if you didn't think so, then we can't be friends. <i>Sorry. That is all.</i><br /><br />Now I'm going back to crying away my swooning heart. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="14482493519141927074" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1458862906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458862906" />
    <a title="Nat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23381142-nat"><img alt="Nat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588309995p2/23381142.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1458862906?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1458862906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10095183546360208166"><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529314308i/25812170.png' width='526' height='251' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><b>or Fate, Time, Television and True Love</b><br/><br/>The funny thing with <strong>
  Landline
</strong> is that I didn’t even fully mean to reread it, I just started the first few pages and then <strong>bang</strong> I was flying through it in true Rainbow Rowell fashion (see: <a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com/2018/03/18/review-fangirl-by-rainbow-rowell-2/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Why I Fangirl over Rainbow Rowell’s Fangirl (Spoilers: Levi)</a>). I felt like I was at an all-you-can-eat buffet, filling myself with one more page, one more...<br/><br/><a href='https://bookspoils.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529314368i/25812171.jpg' width='500' height='337' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='http://bookspoils.tumblr.com/post/174964954723' rel='nofollow noopener'>Source</a><br/><blockquote>As far as time machines go, a magic telephone is pretty useless.<br/><br/>TV writer Georgie McCool can’t actu</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10095183546360208166" style="display:none"><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529314308i/25812170.png" width="526" height="251" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>or Fate, Time, Television and True Love</b><br><br>The funny thing with <strong>
  Landline
</strong> is that I didn’t even fully mean to reread it, I just started the first few pages and then <strong>bang</strong> I was flying through it in true Rainbow Rowell fashion (see: <a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com/2018/03/18/review-fangirl-by-rainbow-rowell-2/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Why I Fangirl over Rainbow Rowell’s Fangirl (Spoilers: Levi)</a>). I felt like I was at an all-you-can-eat buffet, filling myself with one more page, one more...<br><br><a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529314368i/25812171.jpg" width="500" height="337" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://bookspoils.tumblr.com/post/174964954723" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a><br><blockquote>As far as time machines go, a magic telephone is pretty useless.<br><br>TV writer Georgie McCool can’t actually visit the past; all she can do is call it, and hope it picks up. And hope <em>he</em> picks up -- because once Georgie realizes she has a magic phone that calls into the past, all she wants is make things right with her husband, Neal.<br><br>Maybe she can fix the things in their past that seem unfixable in the present. Maybe this stupid phone is giving her a chance to start over. . . . Does Georgie <em>want</em> to start over?<br><br>A heart-wrenching—and hilarious—take on fate, time, television and true love, <em>Landline </em>asks if two people are ever really on the same path, or whether love just means finding someone who will keep meeting you halfway.</blockquote><br>Also funny is the fact when I first read 
  <strong>Landline</strong>
, back in 2015, I came out of it thinking it was my least favorite Rowell book, simply because at that time in my life I couldn't have cared less about married people. But with this reread now, coming after three years, I can't get enough of family-based stories. So I was delighted to discover how with time my perspective had changed and matured to the point of <strong>gobbling up every little detail</strong> concerning the marriage chronicled in here.<br><br>It's so hard to capture all that I loved (because there's so many specifics) but I tried my best by including it all below:<br><br>• Rainbow Rowell's signature humor is ever-present and on-point.<br><br><em>“It was so rare to make Neal laugh. . . .</em><br><em>Georgie used to tease him about being a waste of dimples. “Your face is like an O. Henry story. The world’s sweetest dimples and the boy who never laughs.”</em><br><em>“I laugh.”</em><br><em>“When? When you’re alone?”</em><br><em>“Yeah,” he said. “Every night when I’m sure everyone is asleep, I sit on my bed and laugh maniacally.”</em><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529314263ra/25812161.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was trying to find the best way to describe the humor, when I stumbled upon this <a href="https://tattle.findawayworld.com/author-interview/author-and-narrator-dual-interview-rainbow-rowell-rebecca-lowman/" rel="nofollow noopener">interview</a> between Rainbow Rowell and her audio narrator Rebecca Lowman, discussing the book:<br><br><em>Rowell: "...You know what, I don’t like punchline, sort of zingy humor. So I’m not drawn to comedians who are very big. <strong>I like people who are just sort of talking and they’re funny when they’re talking</strong>. ..."</em><br><br>This. This is exactly it.<br><br>As well as this quote from the book on savoring what we hold precious:<br><br><em>“I put it in my Save Box,” she said.</em><br><em>“What’s that?”</em><br><em>“It’s actually just a box. I, uh . . . <strong>I hate that feeling, you know, when you’re thinking about something you’ve read or heard, and you thought it was so smart at the time, but now you can’t remember it. I save things I don’t want to lose track of</strong>.”</em><br><br>This right here hits the core on why I write such extensive notes during my reading.<br><br>• Georgie's office scenes with Seth (and Scotty) reminded me then why I had such a hard reading this book the first time. They weren't my favorite scenes since no one was shining or bringing anything new to the table. In particular, Seth threw me off my game at the end because I feel like he was flexing, what Reagan in <a href="https://bookspoils.wordpress.com/2018/03/18/review-fangirl-by-rainbow-rowell-2/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Fangirl</a> so lovingly calls, his best friend muscles just to remind everyone that he came first. I'm not a fan. Also: He can't write anything decent down without Georgie around, which makes him a true Nick.<br><br><em>“They were supposed to end up together, Seth and Georgie.</em><br><em>Well, technically, they had ended up together. They’d talked every day since that first day they met.</em><br><em>But they were supposed to end up together-together. Everyone thought it would happen—Georgie had thought it would happen.</em><br><em>Just as soon as Seth exhausted his other possibilities, as soon as he worked through his queue of admirers. He hadn’t been in any hurry, and Georgie didn’t have a say in the matter. She’d taken a number. She was waiting patiently.</em><br><em>And then, one day, she wasn’t.”</em><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529314263ra/25812162.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>• And since we're on the topic of my favorite Rowell book, I was so keen on reading about Neal and Georgie together because it felt like we were seeing Cath and Levi chronicled from Levi's perspective. Georgie is the one initiating all contact with Neal, making sure she can get a laugh out him (at least one), whereas "solid, stolid" Neal is a tough nut to crack, similar to Cath with their difficulty establishing eye contact and needing a barrier between them, such as drawing cartoons (in Cath's case, reading fanfiction out loud) to distract. And lucky for him,<strong> </strong>Georgie doesn’t want the easy thing. To paraphrase <strong>Attachments</strong>, she<b> </b>likes to work a little harder to get the thing she really wants.<br><br><em>“He’s the guy in the Life cereal commercial who hates everything. If Mikey likes you, you know you’re good. If Mikey likes you, it means something.”</em><br><br>• The concept behind 'once we notice something, we see it everywhere' is beyond fascinating to me, so I liked how subtly Rainbow Rowell incorporated that shift between the two:<br><br><em>“How had she missed Neal until junior year? He’d started working at The Spoon as a freshman, same as her. Georgie must have seen him, without really seeing him, dozens of times. Was she that sucked in by Seth? Seth was extra sucky—pushy and loud, always demanding Georgie’s attention. . . .</em><br><em>But once Georgie noticed Neal, she saw him around the office constantly. She’d try not to stare when he walked past her desk on his way to the production room. Sometimes, if she was lucky, he’d look her way and nod.”</em><br><br>Rowell excels at procuring real authentic moments.<br><br><em>“Can we go back and start over?”</em><br><em>“How far back?” Georgie tried to fold her arms, but she was still holding that stupid Zima.</em><br><em>“Back to the wall,” he said. “Back to you walking across the living room toward me. To you saying, ‘I’m surprised to see you here.’”</em><br><em>“Are you saying you want to go back to the living room?”</em><br><em>“No. Just go ahead, say it again now.”</em><br><em>Georgie rolled her eyes, but she said it: “I’m surprised to see you here.”</em><br><em>“You shouldn’t be,” Neal said. He lifted his chin and looked directly in her eyes. For the second time in five minutes. For the second time ever. “I’m here because I knew you’d be here. Because I hoped you would be.”</em><br><br>That moment when people stop playing games (*Gemma Collins echo*) with one another and just present their real selves... Showing someone you're keen on them and having it reciprocated is a grand gesture.<br><br>I equally loved those tiny, intimate moments sprinkled throughout their married life:<br><br><em>“Stop. You’re blowing my mind.”</em><br><em>“Oh, I’ll blow your mind. Girlie.”</em><br><em>“Are you flirting with me?”</em><br><em>He’d turned to her then, pen cap in mouth, and cocked his head. “Yeah. I think so.”</em><br><em>Georgie looked down at her old sweatshirt. At her threadbare yoga pants. “This is what does it for you?”</em><br><em>Neal smiled most of a smile, and the cap fell out of his mouth. “So far.”</em><br><em>Neal . . .”</em><br><br>As well as featuring really beautiful metaphors with flowers, like: <em>“Pizza girl’s name was Alison, and Heather’s face followed her around the room like <strong>a sunflower chasing daylight</strong>.”</em><br><br>And: <em>“(Neal’s face was like <strong>a flower blooming</strong>—you’d need time-lapse photography to really see it in action. But Georgie’d become such a student of his face, she could read most of the twitches.)”</em><br><br>• Regarding the major plot line of the magic telephone, I could only think of <a href="http://bookspoils.tumblr.com/post/174969366473/mihret-i-am-not-letting-anyone-forget-this-vine" rel="nofollow noopener">this vine</a>.<br>To give some background, this quote led me to it:<em> “Georgie exhaled when she heard Neal’s voice, then resisted the urge to ask him who the president was.”</em><br><br>• I've been holding off, but I really have to end on the most epic cameo to appear in this book, featuring my all-time favorite couple: Cath &amp; Levi. I really thought before starting that it wouldn't hit me as hard because I've <strong>already</strong> read it before. But it's been so long and LEVI'S STILL SO GOOD.<br><br><em>“Can we help you find something?” someone said.</em><br><em>Georgie turned. It was the ecstatic young couple. Still hanging on each other, as if neither of them could quite believe the other was finally here.</em><br><em>“Taxi stand?” Georgie said.</em><br><em>“You’re looking for a taxi?” the boy asked. The man. She should probably call him a man. He must be twenty-two, twenty-three; his hair was already thinning.”</em><br><br>My boy is all grown up. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529314263i/25812163.png" alt="bookspoils" width="271" height="266" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><em>“Wait a minute.” The boy got out of the truck, then hopped back inside thirty seconds later with his duffel bag. He unzipped it, and clothes spilled out. He started heaping them in the girl’s lap. “Here,” he said, pulling out a thick, gray wool sweater. “Take this.”</em><br><em>“I can’t take your sweater,” Georgie said.</em><br><em>“Take it. You can mail it back to me—my mom sews my address inside everything. Take it, it’s no big deal.”</em><br><br>LEVI GOES OUT OF HIS WAY TO MAKE SURE GEORGIE GETS SAFELY TO HER DESTINATION (on top of the snowy hill).<br><br>And Cath caught up with Levi's good habits along the way because when they notice Georgie's shoes not having foolproof cover from the Omaha snow, this happens:<br><br><em>“Oh for Christ’s sake,” the girl said. “You can wear my boots.” She reached for the floor. Georgie noticed she was wearing a small engagement ring. “You can have them. I don’t even like them.”</em><br><em>“Absolutely not,” Georgie said. “What if you get stuck in the snow?”</em><br><em>“I’ll be fine,” she said. “<strong>He’d carry me across the city before he let me get my feet wet</strong>.”</em><br><br>Levi would do it in a heartbeat!! <strong>Cue my tears</strong>. <br><br>I really thought that time would pass and one day I would be ready to move on. But these characters are my home, and I’m never going to stop missing them.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529314263ra/25812164.gif" alt="tumblr_omrjbxiu281u4ypbyo4_400" width="268" height="268" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519978783i/25147409.png" alt="Screen Shot 2018-02-28 at 09.46.55" width="110" height="51" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'll close off by sharing this beautiful alternate cover for <strong>
  Landline
</strong>, which has the best details from the book; the Polaroid!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1529314263i/25812165._SY540_.jpg" width="349" height="521" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="https://www.pinterest.com/pin/345721708869342265/" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519978068i/25147363.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519978068i/25147363.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519978068i/25147363.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519978068i/25147363.png" alt="bookspoils" width="35" height="31" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519484203i/25115559.png" width="32" height="32" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Note: I’m an Amazon Affiliate. <div id="review_864733214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/864733214" />
    <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters"><img alt="Elyse  Walters" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514246949p2/597461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/864733214?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elyse  Walters" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elyse  Walters" href="/user/show/597461-elyse-walters">Elyse  Walters</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer864733214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17134734867029112806">I saw a friend reading this book just now - and remembered I read it early last year. Since it won "BEST FICTION" on Goodreads in 2014.....I figured then it must be worth a $1.99. ...( the sale price at the time). <br/>It was sooooo 'fair' that when I saw that my overdrive library had it available, too, - I thought it might be better as an audio -- afterall - the name of the book is called "Landline".<br/><br/>Well- reading it - or listening to it - I enjoyed this conversation ( the story), for about as long a</span>
  <span id="freeText17134734867029112806" style="display:none">I saw a friend reading this book just now - and remembered I read it early last year. Since it won "BEST FICTION" on Goodreads in 2014.....I figured then it must be worth a $1.99. ...( the sale price at the time). <br />It was sooooo 'fair' that when I saw that my overdrive library had it available, too, - I thought it might be better as an audio -- afterall - the name of the book is called "Landline".<br /><br />Well- reading it - or listening to it - I enjoyed this conversation ( the story), for about as long as I do many phone conversations: Enjoyable for awhile - nice connecting with my friends - even up to two hours is 'great'.... not bad ... but any longer than 2 hours, I'm ready to set the landline down! <br /><br />Can anyone tell me WHY .......THIS book won BEST FICTION? It's a mystery to me! <br />Even if .....'if'.......( and that won't be me ), a reader gave it 5 stars -- did they really believe this was the best fiction of the year? It's almost as shocking as this years Presidential election. <br /><br />One thing I 'did' enjoy about this story - right off the bat....'was' the line of communication choice.<br />Evening conversations-OVER THE TELEPHONE- not skype - not texting- took place <br />between Neal and Georgie. I liked the pure symbolism of what the landline phone with the twirly cord represents to me. I liked enjoying my own memories. <br /><br />I use to speak on my princess landline phone for hours a night during 8th grade. Ron and I talked on the phone. We did our homework over the landline - ate our snacks - talked about music -school gossip - our families - and strengthen our relationship. I wore his ring around my neck all year long. We're still friends today.<br /><br />When I would see Ron at school during the day back in 8th grade- we barely talked to one another. He sat with the 'boys'. Me with the 'girls'. One day I got tired of the segregation---( He was the greatest on the telephone each night) -- but stepping over the line to the boys side during lunch was off limits to girls. Enough was enough. One day - I got so mad -- walked across the invisible <br />WALL OF DO NOT ENTER..... and threw my ring at him. [years later- we laugh about it... I said I was sorry - but he said he deserved it] ....<br /><br />The only problem was --- BACK in 8th grade - I lost too, by getting mad -- I lost my wonderful evening landline phone chats.... with my best friend. <br /><br />The LANDLINE with the wiggly long cord had many memories for many of us old farts. <br /><br />But now with texting, email, and Facebook - most of us don't even own a landline anymore. Different memories! <br /><br />There were parts of this story that went - FLAT - but I like what Rainbow was trying to do. Her overall message was sincere and valuable. Take time to really connect with the person we love most - The Landline was a magical tool in supporting a married couple find their hearts back to each other. <br /><br />Resentments were stacking up.... (their jobs, kids, required demands).....<br />So..... a little 'fairy tale' type story takes over.... Georgie begins to connect - by landline- when Neal is away on business - not just with her old raga muffin husband, instead she gets the 'younger' Neal.... the guy she first fell in love with. <br />It's a cute idea ... enjoyable 'enough'... but Best fiction? Now that's funny! <br /><br />3 stars for a solid. "I liked enough". A few great ideas that went flat. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17134734867029112806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2403829279" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2403829279" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2403829279?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2403829279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11448543994104234468">i have to hand it to rainbow rowell. even though her books tend to be a hit or near miss for me, i think its very neat how, across four books, she has managed to effortlessly capture what it means to live during four different stages of life - high school, college, working/dating young adult, and working/married adult. really kinda cool if you think about it. and even though this was one of those near misses for me, it still was a really cute story. <br/><br/>the writing in this is classic rainbow rowell.</span>
  <span id="freeText11448543994104234468" style="display:none">i have to hand it to rainbow rowell. even though her books tend to be a hit or near miss for me, i think its very neat how, across four books, she has managed to effortlessly capture what it means to live during four different stages of life - high school, college, working/dating young adult, and working/married adult. really kinda cool if you think about it. and even though this was one of those near misses for me, it still was a really cute story. <br /><br />the writing in this is classic rainbow rowell. theres a very light quality to the way she tells her stories, which makes it so easy to breeze through her books. so whilst her writing was really refreshing to read again, i think the story fell a little short with its protagonist. she just wasnt likable? like, at all. i get that sometimes you have to have an unlikable character because not everyone can be happy and lovely all the time, but it was quite difficult to read about a character so selfish. also, there were quite a few loose ends towards the end of this which is a little of of character for rowells books.<br /><br />overall, i did think this had a good message. but its hard to appreciate that message when it happening to a character you dont really care for. im glad i read it, but definitely not her best work, in my opinion. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11448543994104234468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781409154914" href="/book/show/21869936-landline">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1074899824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2062074351413119486">Gosh, rereading this book again was so fulfilling. I forgot how incredibly inventive and unique Rainbow Rowell’s writing was. How wholesome her characters are how wholesome reading the whole story felt. <br/><br/>It’s a love story. It’s about a marriage that is on the brink of failure and the characters holding on to the remaining scraps of their marriage. Do you give up your career to save your marriage or not? What’s more important? What ultimately brings you happiness? <br/><br/>Everything about it felt so real </span>
  <span id="freeText2062074351413119486" style="display:none">Gosh, rereading this book again was so fulfilling. I forgot how incredibly inventive and unique Rainbow Rowell’s writing was. How wholesome her characters are how wholesome reading the whole story felt. <br /><br />It’s a love story. It’s about a marriage that is on the brink of failure and the characters holding on to the remaining scraps of their marriage. Do you give up your career to save your marriage or not? What’s more important? What ultimately brings you happiness? <br /><br />Everything about it felt so real and raw. But with Rowell’s humour infused in the story, it was easy to get through and magical to get read. I didn’t want it to end. <br />_________________________________<br /><br /><b>Initial review:</b><br />Rowell, never stop writing. Please? Thank you. <br /><br />Bloody perfection!</span>

Because Georgie is a comedy writer and has to work on a show. I don't get the hype around this one - wasn't worth the read and I'm glad I didn't purchase it.</span>

    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1445479149?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/39880206-mac-dubista-keso-the-bibliobibuli-v">Mac Dubista Keso The Bibliobibuli v(=∩_∩=)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=definitely-not-young-adult">definitely-not-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=with-a-touch-of-paranormal">with-a-touch-of-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=easy-read">easy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1445479149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2516379154557918599"><b> Not quite three stars but almost there.^^ </b><br/><br/>	Oh wow! I never thought I’d say this of a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4208569.Rainbow_Rowell' title='Rainbow Rowell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rainbow Rowell</a> novel but my reading experience with this one bordered between a little “meh” and sort of “like”. It’s interesting because it’s a story about an old yellow landline that magically lets 2013 Georgie talk to her husband, Neal, in his 1998 version. It’s a little “meh” because after more than 310 pages, nothing big really happened. <br/><br/>	Georgie and Neal’s marriage is at the brink of falling off the cliff</span>
  <span id="freeText2516379154557918599" style="display:none"><b> Not quite three stars but almost there.^^ </b><br /><br />	Oh wow! I never thought I’d say this of a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4208569.Rainbow_Rowell" title="Rainbow Rowell" rel="nofollow noopener">Rainbow Rowell</a> novel but my reading experience with this one bordered between a little “meh” and sort of “like”. It’s interesting because it’s a story about an old yellow landline that magically lets 2013 Georgie talk to her husband, Neal, in his 1998 version. It’s a little “meh” because after more than 310 pages, nothing big really happened. <br /><br />	Georgie and Neal’s marriage is at the brink of falling off the cliff. Georgie clearly knows the cause but she still lets Neal and her two wonderful little girls go off to Omaha for their supposedly family Christmas break without her because of her job. As a consequence, she couldn’t work well which kind of defeats the purpose of her sacrificial stay. Depressed and worried, Georgie stays at her mom’s house while her family is away. In her old room is the old yellow phone that lets her talk to her 1998 Neal that basically sums up the majority of the plot.<br /><br />	It’s appealing because the author has this inherent writing ability to make any story easy to read but a little disappointing because for a story that is supposed to be magical, there wasn’t any real spark about the characters and their relationships. The supposedly magical object wasn’t really substantial to the story. To me, it only felt like an accessory to add something surreal. I was waiting for a huge epiphanic moment for Georgie but in the end, she simply does what she knows she was supposed to do a long time ago. With or without magic time travel phone, she easily would have still reached such a realization. <br /><br />	I know I’ve been sounding like a really annoying pessimist lately, it’s probably this reading slump that has settled deep in my muscles which I just refuse to acknowledge because I still couldn’t let go of this delusion that I’m immune to this terrible disease. :(<br /><br />	<b> On the bright side, it’s still an easy, light read for the approaching Holidays. Also, I have always been a fan of Rowell’s writing and that’ll always be a plus!^^ </b>	<br /><br />Lookin' for reviews with more positive vibes? Check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1189230955?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Mac's</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1032482229?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Gi's</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2516379154557918599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16978055467703014101" style="display:none">Meow! Ah, Rainbow Rowell, you have stolen my heart yet again. Another beautiful, heartfelt, emotionally rewarding, and insanely hilarious novel from start to finish. This book made me smile. Rowell's novels are like comfort food. They always make you feel warm and happy inside. Georgie McCool, you're one crazy nut, and Neal, you're the coolest little hobbit I ever did know. lol I enjoyed reading about Georgie and Neal's backstory as a couple. Rowell's various characters are relatable, quirky, sincere, and always a joy to read. Enjoy, fellow goodreaders! P.S. Now where can I get myself a magic telephone??? lol </span>

<div id="review_955469879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955469879" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955469879?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer955469879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6869331158698648232"><i>Landline</i> is different from what I expected: first of all it's an adult book which I only realized when I started it, but this is totally my fault and also not a bad thing. I was due for an adult book. And, unlike her usual contemporary reads, this one has a bit of a paranormal vibe to it. I'm not sure how I felt about this at first, I loved the mind-f*ck nature of it, but it has an element that very rarely impresses me <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[[time-travel] <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, so I was afraid of the directio</span>
  <span id="freeText6869331158698648232" style="display:none"><i>Landline</i> is different from what I expected: first of all it's an adult book which I only realized when I started it, but this is totally my fault and also not a bad thing. I was due for an adult book. And, unlike her usual contemporary reads, this one has a bit of a paranormal vibe to it. I'm not sure how I felt about this at first, I loved the mind-f*ck nature of it, but it has an element that very rarely impresses me <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[[time-travel] <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, so I was afraid of the direction it was going in. In the end, though, I can say I quite enjoyed the story. It has a bit of a fairy-tale quality to it, so have to go into it with an open mind, but it's a wonderfully romantic journey that makes you stop and remember why you chose this life for yourself in the first place. May it be a marriage, a career, a hometown, you chose it for a reason. You were happy, maybe even passionate about these decisions once, but when things are hard it's sometimes difficult to remember why. <br><br>What I know from Rainbow Rowell is that she knows how to craft realistic and wonderfully flawed characters, who are so easy to connect and relate to. Georgie's marriage is crumbling, and she feels as if she's losing it all - even her mind. Through flashbacks along with Georgie's independent and determined personality, we get to see her fall in love. Not just with her now husband, but also with her best friend and career. We got to see what led her to choose this life for herself. How happy she was back then, and how life got in the way since. Even though she's not always especially likeable, she has this effortless narrative voice, peppered with humour, that makes it easy to fly through the pages. <br><br>Aside from Georgie, every single secondary character is painted with such memorable qualities. Her sister, Heather, and her best friend Seth, quickly became my favorites. The latter for his sarcasm and liveliness, the former for her fun-loving personality and sisterly devotion. Even the smallest of roles - like the pizza delivery person and Neal's mother - felt authentic and added to the overall charm of the story. <br><br>This is a romance through and through. It's about a woman who needs to make a though decision to save her marriage. It's a story that so many will be able to relate to. Juggling between a career and home life is never easy and, often, sacrifices need to be made, and dreams are not achieved. In the end, despite the "perfect" ending, I was left feeling uncertain towards the lasting quality of their relationship. I'm not even 100% sure I was rooting for them all along, to be honest. I definitely don't agree with every decision Georgie did - she can be selfish, especially when it comes to her relationship with Seth, but Rowell does make us understand why it's hard for her to let go. <br><br>This book touches on love and family, but also on guilt and self-worth. It's a novel that paints realistic relationships, not idealistic ones. Because in reality, romance is rarely idealistic, and with many things in life, it's only worth as much as the effort you put in.<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6869331158698648232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1357910318235234841" style="display:none"><b>2nd Read</b> <i>March 2019</i><br /><br />Rainbow Rowell has this way of writing that <b>makes me not want to blink.</b> I read and read and read until I hear the birds chirping and realise - <i>oh shit the sun is rising.</i> <br /><br />This is a book about a marriage on the rocks. It's also about how Georgie and Neal met, fell in love and how they got to where they are now. <br /><br />Separated for the Christmas season, Georgie knows that she has to do something to repair what is broken between them. But that's hard to do when Neal is half way across the country. He call her and she calls him but for some reason they keep missing each other and Georgie's cell phone is giving her problems. She decides to use the old Landline at her moms house and is finally able to get through to Neal... But it turns out it's the Neal she knew 15 years before. <br /><br />This book was just so beautiful and Neal and Georgie's chemistry blew me away even more this time around. I enjoy books about struggling marriages. Not all marriages are easy or the same and it's interesting to me the way couples repair their relationship. <br /><br /><b>1st Read</b> <i>February 2018</i><br /><br />Holy shit. This was amazing. I am in awe of Rainbow Rowell's mastery. This might be my favourite of hers. Who am I kidding. I can't even compare her books they're all fucking brilliant. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1129214367" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1129214367" />
    <a title="Cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9728092-cat"><img alt="Cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346272035p2/9728092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1129214367?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cat" href="/user/show/9728092-cat">Cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/22796453-landline">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9728092-cat?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9728092-cat?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1129214367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16155895538746268737">I always find it quite a shame when the concept of a book is thwarted by its development. Like the author came up with a great idea for a book but wasn't able to write down a story up to the standards of that idea.<br/><br/>That's what I feel that happened with 'Landline'. The idea that somebody in the present could talk with someone from the past over a landline phone sounds really interesting. The way Rowell spun her story around this idea was not so.<br/><br/>A thirty seven year-old woman named Georgie McCool ch</span>
  <span id="freeText16155895538746268737" style="display:none">I always find it quite a shame when the concept of a book is thwarted by its development. Like the author came up with a great idea for a book but wasn't able to write down a story up to the standards of that idea.<br /><br />That's what I feel that happened with 'Landline'. The idea that somebody in the present could talk with someone from the past over a landline phone sounds really interesting. The way Rowell spun her story around this idea was not so.<br /><br />A thirty seven year-old woman named Georgie McCool chooses her work as a sitcom writer (or whatever Georgie does for a living) over spending Christmas in Omaha with her husband Neal and their two daughters Alice and Noomi (whose real name is actually Naomi). As a matter of fact, Georgie always chooses her work over everything else. And Neal just drags along, without saying anything. He is the stay-at-home dad and Georgie spends her life working. But it's Christmas, they are supposed to go to Omaha and Neal boards the plane with his daughters, leaving Georgie in sunny California with her work. Then, as Georgia starts realising Neal is not even calling her and that might mean he's upset with her, she decides to make a move and calls him. Only to discover that getting in touch with her husband via mobile phone is quite impossible. So she moves to her old yellow rotary phone, the one she used to use as a young woman, in her mother's house. Back when she was dating Neal. And Georgie is able to get in touch with her husband, only that the Neal on the other side on the line isn't the actual Neal. He is the Neal from 1998, the Neal Georgie dated back then. Her boyfriend Neal. And so it follows a series of over-the-phone between actual Georgie and 1998 Neal, while Georgie tries to understand what is the meaning of all that and what is she supposed to do to fix the present situation.<br /><br />Boring. This book is boring. And I liked the idea. But I didn't like Georgie, I couldn't feel sorry for her, and what's with those over-the-phone conversations?! I couldn't care for them, especially because they didn't bring any insight to the story. In the end, Georgie understands what she has to do. But, duh!, was there any need for those conversations with Neal from the past? I found them completely useless and confusing. Especially given the rushed-up end.<br /><br />And Neal... Is he supposed to be a likeable character? A man that seldom smiles? A man who has this weird laugh? A huff? Is that supposed to be cute? And all that talk about his dimples. Gosh! Neal has dimples but doesn't smile. Great. Every woman dream guy.<br /><br />Another this that irked me what the way Rainbow Rowell got her characters, especially Georgie, to talk. Great for a YA story, but not so great for a thirty seven year old woman to talk. Because Georgie talked like that. She even used "like" in the middle of her sentences. It's kind of creepy. It's something I can tolerate in YA, but not in a story with adult characters, who are older than me.<br /><br />And is 'Landline' supposed to be a book about the management of a crumbling-to-pieces marriage? Because nothing really happens in that direction. Georgie spends the time whining about the situation of her marriage and talking on the phone with her boyfriend from 1998. And Neal, truthful to himself, just stays in Omaha. He does nothing. There is virtually no talk between Georgie and Neal about what they are going through. And when I say "Georgie and Neal", I mean "Georgie and Neal" from the present. That doesn't happen and it made me feel like this book was a waste of words.<br /><br />Which is a shame. I like Rowell's writing and this could've been such a great book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16155895538746268737" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_946349616" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/946349616" />
    <a title="Elisabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13130014-elisabeth"><img alt="Elisabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563906743p2/13130014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/946349616?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elisabeth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elisabeth" href="/user/show/13130014-elisabeth">Elisabeth</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
